        <div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" dir="ltr" lang="en">
         <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
          American businessman (born 1984)
         </div>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">
          .mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}
         </style>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          "Zuckerberg" redirects here. For other uses, see
          <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Zuckerberg_(disambiguation)" title="Zuckerberg (disambiguation)">
           Zuckerberg (disambiguation)
          </a>
          .
         </div>

               <li class="nv-talk">
                <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Meta_sidebar" title="Template talk:Meta sidebar">
                 <abbr title="Discuss this template">
                  t
                 </abbr>
                </a>
               </li>
               <li class="nv-edit">
                <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Meta_sidebar" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Meta sidebar">
                 <abbr title="Edit this template">
                  e
                 </abbr>
                </a>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </div>
            </td>
           </tr>
          </tbody>
         </table>
         <p>
          <b>
           Mark Elliot Zuckerberg
          </b>
          (
          <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap">
           <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa">
            <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
             /
             <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
              <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
               ˈ
              </span>
              <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
               z
              </span>
              <span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">
               ʌ
              </span>
              <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
               k
              </span>
              <span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">
               ər
              </span>
              <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
               b
              </span>
              <span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">
               ɜːr
              </span>
              <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
               ɡ
              </span>
             </span>
             /
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
          ; born May 14, 1984) is an American businessman. He co-founded the social media service
          <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
           Facebook
          </a>
          and its parent company
          <a href="/wiki/Meta_Platforms" title="Meta Platforms">
           Meta Platforms
          </a>
          (formerly Facebook, Inc.), of which he is chairman, chief executive officer and controlling shareholder.
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg briefly attended
          <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">
           Harvard University
          </a>
          , where he launched Facebook in February 2004 with his roommates
          <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Saverin" title="Eduardo Saverin">
           Eduardo Saverin
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Andrew_McCollum" title="Andrew McCollum">
           Andrew McCollum
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Moskovitz" title="Dustin Moskovitz">
           Dustin Moskovitz
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hughes" title="Chris Hughes">
           Chris Hughes
          </a>
          . Zuckerberg took the
          <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering_of_Facebook" title="Initial public offering of Facebook">
           company public in May 2012
          </a>
          with majority shares. In 2008, at age 23, he became the world's youngest self-made billionaire. He has since used his funds to organize multiple donations, including the establishment of the
          <a href="/wiki/Chan_Zuckerberg_Initiative" title="Chan Zuckerberg Initiative">
           Chan Zuckerberg Initiative
          </a>
          . His net worth as of June 13, 2024 is
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">
           USD
          </a>
          $176 billion, making him the fourth richest person in the world, behind
          <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">
           Elon Musk
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Arnault" title="Bernard Arnault">
           Bernard Arnault
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">
           Jeff Bezos
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-1">
            [1]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          A film depicting Zuckerberg's early career, legal troubles and initial success with Facebook,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">
            The Social Network
           </a>
          </i>
          , was released in 2010 and won multiple
          <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">
           Academy Awards
          </a>
          . His prominence and fast rise in the technology industry has prompted political and legal attention. The founding of Facebook involved Zuckerberg in multiple lawsuits regarding the creation and ownership of the website as well as issues of user privacy.
         </p>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">
          .mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}
         </style>
         <div class="toclimit-3">
          <meta property="mw:PageProp/toc"/>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Early_life_and_education">
           Early life and education
          </h2>
         </div>
         <p>
          Mark Elliot Zuckerberg was born on May 14, 1984, in
          <a href="/wiki/White_Plains,_New_York" title="White Plains, New York">
           White Plains, New York
          </a>
          to psychiatrist Karen (
          <span title="Name at birth">
           <a href="/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names" title="Birth name">
            née
           </a>
           Kempner
          </span>
          ) and dentist Edward Zuckerberg.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-2">
            [2]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
           <a href="#cite_note-3">
            [3]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He and his three sisters (Arielle,
          <a href="/wiki/Randi_Zuckerberg" title="Randi Zuckerberg">
           Randi
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Donna_Zuckerberg" title="Donna Zuckerberg">
           Donna
          </a>
          ) were raised in a
          <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">
           Reform Jewish
          </a>
          household
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haartez_4-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Haartez-4">
            [4]
           </a>
          </sup>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Dobbs_Ferry,_New_York" title="Dobbs Ferry, New York">
           Dobbs Ferry, New York
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          His great-grandparents were emigrants from Austria, Germany, and Poland.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
           <a href="#cite_note-6">
            [6]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg initially attended
          <a href="/wiki/Ardsley_High_School" title="Ardsley High School">
           Ardsley High School
          </a>
          before transferring to
          <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Exeter_Academy" title="Phillips Exeter Academy">
           Phillips Exeter Academy
          </a>
          . He was captain of the fencing team.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirkpatrick_7-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Kirkpatrick-7">
            [7]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
           <a href="#cite_note-8">
            [8]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Software_development">
           Software development
          </h3>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading4">
          <h4 id="Early_years">
           Early years
          </h4>
         </div>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg began using computers and writing software in middle school. In high school, he built a program that allowed all the computers between his house and his father's dental office to communicate with each other.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
           <a href="#cite_note-9">
            [9]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
           <a href="#cite_note-10">
            [10]
           </a>
          </sup>
          During Zuckerberg's high-school years, he worked to build a music player called the Synapse Media Player. The device used
          <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">
           machine learning
          </a>
          to learn the user's listening habits, which was posted to
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Slashdot" title="Slashdot">
            Slashdot
           </a>
          </i>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
           <a href="#cite_note-11">
            [11]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and received a rating of 3 out of 5 from
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" title="PC Magazine">
            PC Magazine
           </a>
          </i>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
           <a href="#cite_note-12">
            [12]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">
            The New Yorker
           </a>
          </i>
          once said of Zuckerberg: "some kids played computer games. Mark created them".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          While still in high school, he attended
          <a href="/wiki/Mercy_University" title="Mercy University">
           Mercy College
          </a>
          taking a graduate computer course on Thursday evenings.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading4">
          <h4 id="College_years">
           College years
          </h4>
         </div>
         <p>
          The
          <i>
           New Yorker
          </i>
          noted that by the time Zuckerberg began classes at
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard">
           Harvard
          </a>
          in 2002, he had already achieved a "reputation as a programming prodigy".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-3">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He studied
          <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">
           psychology
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">
           computer science
          </a>
          ,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
           <a href="#cite_note-13">
            [13]
           </a>
          </sup>
          resided in
          <a href="/wiki/Kirkland_House" title="Kirkland House">
           Kirkland House
          </a>
          ,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
           <a href="#cite_note-14">
            [14]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and belonged to
          <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">
           Alpha Epsilon Pi
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-4">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In his second year, he wrote a program that he called CourseMatch, which allowed users to make class selection decisions based on the choices of other students and help them form study groups.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
           <a href="#cite_note-15">
            [15]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Later, he created a different program he initially called
          <a href="/wiki/History_of_Facebook#FaceMash" title="History of Facebook">
           Facemash
          </a>
          that let students select the best-looking person from a choice of photos. Arie Hasit, Zuckerberg's roommate at the time, explained:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           We had books called Face Books, which included the names and pictures of everyone who lived in the student dorms. At first, he built a site and placed two pictures or pictures of two males and two females. Visitors to the site had to choose who was "hotter" and according to the votes there would be a ranking.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasit_16-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-Hasit-16">
             [16]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          The site went up over a weekend, but by Monday morning, the college shut it down, because its popularity had overwhelmed one of Harvard's
          <a href="/wiki/Network_switch" title="Network switch">
           network switches
          </a>
          preventing students from accessing the Internet.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
           <a href="#cite_note-17">
            [17]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In addition, many students complained that their photos were being used without permission. Zuckerberg apologized publicly, and the student paper ran articles stating that his site was "completely improper".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasit_16-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Hasit-16">
            [16]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Career">
           Career
          </h2>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Facebook">
           Facebook
          </h3>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Further information:
          <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
           Facebook
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/History_of_Facebook" title="History of Facebook">
           History of Facebook
          </a>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1229112069" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <table class="infobox" style="width: 210px; clear: right; float:right;margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em">
          <tbody>
           <tr>
            <th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="font-size:115%">
             External videos
            </th>
           </tr>
           <tr>
            <td class="infobox-image" colspan="2">
             <span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File">
              <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:YouTube_Logo_2017.svg">
               <img alt="YouTube logo" class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="114" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/YouTube_Logo_2017.svg/90px-YouTube_Logo_2017.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/YouTube_Logo_2017.svg/135px-YouTube_Logo_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/YouTube_Logo_2017.svg/180px-YouTube_Logo_2017.svg.png 2x" width="90"/>
              </a>
             </span>
            </td>
           </tr>
           <tr>
            <td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2" style="text-align: left">
             <span typeof="mw:File">
              <span>
               <img alt="video icon" class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>
              </span>
             </span>
             <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KerxaaZVoCY" rel="nofollow">
              "Mark Zuckerberg's career in 90 seconds | Tech Gurus"
             </a>
             via
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">
               The Daily Telegraph
              </a>
             </i>
             <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele90_18-0">
              <a href="#cite_note-tele90-18">
               [18]
              </a>
             </sup>
            </td>
           </tr>
          </tbody>
         </table>
         <p>
          In January 2004, Zuckerberg began writing code for a new website.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman,_Claire2_19-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Hoffman,_Claire2-19">
            [19]
           </a>
          </sup>
          On February 4, 2004, Zuckerberg launched "Thefacebook", originally located at thefacebook.com, in partnership with his roommates
          <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Saverin" title="Eduardo Saverin">
           Eduardo Saverin
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Andrew_McCollum" title="Andrew McCollum">
           Andrew McCollum
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Moskovitz" title="Dustin Moskovitz">
           Dustin Moskovitz
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hughes" title="Chris Hughes">
           Chris Hughes
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skepticism2_20-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-skepticism2-20">
            [20]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rww051009_21-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-rww051009-21">
            [21]
           </a>
          </sup>
          An earlier inspiration for Facebook may have come from
          <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Exeter_Academy" title="Phillips Exeter Academy">
           Phillips Exeter Academy
          </a>
          , the prep school from which Zuckerberg graduated in 2002. It published its own student directory, "The Photo Address Book", which students referred to as "The Facebook". Such photo directories were an important part of the student social experience at many private schools. With them, students were able to list attributes such as their class years, their friends, and their telephone numbers.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rww051009_21-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-rww051009-21">
            [21]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg">
           <img alt="Mark Zuckerberg with a laptop, facing the camera" class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="399" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg/220px-MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg/330px-MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/MarkZuckerberg-crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           Zuckerberg in 2005
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          Six days after the site launched, three Harvard seniors,
          <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Winklevoss" title="Cameron Winklevoss">
           Cameron Winklevoss
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Winklevoss" title="Tyler Winklevoss">
           Tyler Winklevoss
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Divya_Narendra" title="Divya Narendra">
           Divya Narendra
          </a>
          , accused Zuckerberg of intentionally misleading them into believing that he would help them build a social network called
          <a href="/wiki/ConnectU" title="ConnectU">
           HarvardConnection.com
          </a>
          , when he was using their ideas to build a competing product.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zuckerberghacked2_22-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-zuckerberghacked2-22">
            [22]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The three complained to
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Harvard_Crimson" title="The Harvard Crimson">
            The Harvard Crimson
           </a>
          </i>
          , and the newspaper began an investigation in response. While Zuckerberg tried to convince the editors not to run the story,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
           <a href="#cite_note-23">
            [23]
           </a>
          </sup>
          he also broke into two of the editors' email accounts—for which he made use of their private login data logs from TheFacebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
           <a href="#cite_note-24">
            [24]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
           <a href="#cite_note-25">
            [25]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Following the official launch of the Facebook social media platform, the three filed a lawsuit against Zuckerberg that resulted in a settlement.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytb2_26-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-nytb2-26">
            [26]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The agreed settlement was for 1.2 million Facebook shares and $20 million in cash.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
           <a href="#cite_note-27">
            [27]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg's Facebook started off as just a "Harvard thing" until he decided to spread it to other schools, enlisting the help of roommate and co-founder
          <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Moskovitz" title="Dustin Moskovitz">
           Dustin Moskovitz
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
           <a href="#cite_note-28">
            [28]
           </a>
          </sup>
          They began with
          <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
           Columbia University
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">
           New York University
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">
           Stanford University
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">
           Dartmouth College
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">
           Cornell University
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">
           University of Pennsylvania
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">
           Brown University
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">
           Yale University
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
           <a href="#cite_note-29">
            [29]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg dropped out of Harvard in his sophomore year in order to complete the project.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
           <a href="#cite_note-30">
            [30]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg, Moskovitz and the other co-founders moved to
          <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">
           Palo Alto, California
          </a>
          , where they leased a small house that served as an office. Over the summer, Zuckerberg met
          <a href="/wiki/Peter_Thiel" title="Peter Thiel">
           Peter Thiel
          </a>
          , who invested in his company. They got their first office in mid-2004. According to Zuckerberg, the group planned to return to Harvard, but eventually decided to remain in California, where Zuckerberg appreciated the "mythical place" of
          <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">
           Silicon Valley
          </a>
          , the center of computer technology in California.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
           <a href="#cite_note-31">
            [31]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
           <a href="#cite_note-32">
            [32]
           </a>
          </sup>
          They had already turned down offers by major corporations to buy the company. In an interview in 2007, Zuckerberg explained his reasoning: "It's not because of the amount of money. For me and my colleagues, the most important thing is that we create an open information flow for people. Having media corporations owned by
          <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">
           conglomerates
          </a>
          is just not an attractive idea to me".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exeter_33-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Exeter-33">
            [33]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The same year, speaking at
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y_Combinator_Inc" title="Y Combinator Inc">
           Y Combinator
          </a>
          's
          <i>
           Startup School
          </i>
          course at
          <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">
           Stanford University
          </a>
          , Zuckerberg made a
          <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">
           controversial assertion
          </a>
          that "young people are just smarter" and that other entrepreneurs should bias towards hiring young people.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
           <a href="#cite_note-34">
            [34]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          He restated these goals to
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">
            Wired
           </a>
          </i>
          magazine in 2010: "The thing I really care about is the mission, making the world open".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired-zuckerberg_35-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-wired-zuckerberg-35">
            [35]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Earlier, in April 2009, Zuckerberg had sought the advice of former
          <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">
           Netscape
          </a>
          CFO
          <a href="/wiki/Peter_Currie_(businessman)" title="Peter Currie (businessman)">
           Peter Currie
          </a>
          regarding financing strategies for Facebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsOctBPP_36-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-twsOctBPP-36">
            [36]
           </a>
          </sup>
          On July 21, 2010, Zuckerberg reported that Facebook had reached the 500-million-user mark.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
           <a href="#cite_note-37">
            [37]
           </a>
          </sup>
          When asked whether Facebook could earn more income from advertising as a result of its phenomenal growth, he explained:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           I guess we could ... If you look at how much of our page is taken up with ads compared to the average
           <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_marketing" title="Search engine marketing">
            search
           </a>
           query. The average for us is a little less than 10 percent of the pages and the average for search is about 20 percent taken up with ads ... That's the simplest thing we could do. But we aren't like that. We make enough money. Right, I mean, we are keeping things running; we are growing at the rate we want to.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired-zuckerberg_35-1">
            <a href="#cite_note-wired-zuckerberg-35">
             [35]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          In 2010,
          <a href="/wiki/Steven_Levy" title="Steven Levy">
           Steven Levy
          </a>
          , who wrote the 1984 book
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Hackers:_Heroes_of_the_Computer_Revolution" title="Hackers: Heroes of the Computer Revolution">
            Hackers: Heroes of the Computer Revolution
           </a>
          </i>
          , wrote that Zuckerberg "clearly thinks of himself as a
          <a href="/wiki/Hacker_culture" title="Hacker culture">
           hacker
          </a>
          ". Zuckerberg said that "it's OK to break things" "to make them better".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired041910_38-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-wired041910-38">
            [38]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fast092410_39-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fast092410-39">
            [39]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Facebook instituted "
          <a href="/wiki/Hackathon" title="Hackathon">
           hackathons
          </a>
          " held every six to eight weeks where participants would have one night to conceive of and complete a project.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired041910_38-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-wired041910-38">
            [38]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The company provided music, food, and beer at the hackathons, and many Facebook staff members, including Zuckerberg, regularly attended.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fast092410_39-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-fast092410-39">
            [39]
           </a>
          </sup>
          "The idea is that you can build something really good in a night", Zuckerberg told Levy. "And that's part of the personality of Facebook now ... It's definitely very core to my personality".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired041910_38-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-wired041910-38">
            [38]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2007, Zuckerberg was added to
          <a href="/wiki/MIT_Technology_Review" title="MIT Technology Review">
           MIT Technology Review
          </a>
          's
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TR35" title="TR35">
           TR35
          </a>
          list as one of the top 35 innovators in the world under the age of 35.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
           <a href="#cite_note-40">
            [40]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">
            Vanity Fair
           </a>
          </i>
          magazine named Zuckerberg number 1 on its 2010 list of the Top 100 "most influential people of the
          <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">
           Information Age
          </a>
          ".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
           <a href="#cite_note-41">
            [41]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg ranked number 23 on the
          <i>
           Vanity Fair
          </i>
          100 list in 2009.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
           <a href="#cite_note-42">
            [42]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In 2010, Zuckerberg was chosen as number 16 in
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">
            New Statesman
           </a>
          </i>
          <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
           '
          </span>
          s annual survey of the world's 50 most influential figures.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htanna_43-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-htanna-43">
            [43]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In a 2011 interview with
          <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">
           PBS
          </a>
          shortly after the death of
          <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">
           Steve Jobs
          </a>
          , Zuckerberg said that Jobs had advised him on how to create a management team at Facebook that was "focused on building as high quality and good things as you are".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
           <a href="#cite_note-44">
            [44]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="3060" data-file-width="4092" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg/220px-Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg/330px-Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg/440px-Medvedev_and_Zuckerberg_October_2012-1.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           Zuckerberg and Russian Prime Minister
           <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
            Dmitry Medvedev
           </a>
           during their meeting at the Russian leader's residence outside Moscow, October 1, 2012
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          On October 1, 2012, Zuckerberg met with then Russian Prime Minister
          <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
           Dmitry Medvedev
          </a>
          in Moscow to stimulate social media innovation in Russia and to boost Facebook's position in the Russian market.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
           <a href="#cite_note-45">
            [45]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
           <a href="#cite_note-46">
            [46]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Russia's communications minister tweeted that Medvedev persuaded Zuckerberg to open a research center in Moscow instead of trying to lure away Russian programmers. In 2012, Facebook had roughly 9 million users in Russia, while domestic clone
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VK_(social_networking)" title="VK (social networking)">
           VK
          </a>
          had around 34 million.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
           <a href="#cite_note-47">
            [47]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
           <a href="#cite_note-48">
            [48]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Rebecca Van Dyck, Facebook's head of consumer marketing, said that 85 million American Facebook users were exposed to the first day of the Home promotional campaign on April 6, 2013.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
           <a href="#cite_note-49">
            [49]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On August 19, 2013,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">
            The Washington Post
           </a>
          </i>
          reported that Zuckerberg's Facebook profile was hacked by an unemployed web developer.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
           <a href="#cite_note-50">
            [50]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          At the 2013
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TechCrunch_Disrupt" title="TechCrunch Disrupt">
           TechCrunch Disrupt
          </a>
          conference, held in September, Zuckerberg stated that he was working towards registering the 5 billion people who were not connected to the Internet as of the conference on Facebook. Zuckerberg then explained that this is intertwined with the aim of the
          <a href="/wiki/Internet.org" title="Internet.org">
           Internet.org
          </a>
          project, whereby Facebook, with the support of other technology companies, seeks to increase the number of people connected to the internet.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Six_51-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Six-51">
            [51]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sew_52-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Sew-52">
            [52]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg was the keynote speaker at the 2014
          <a href="/wiki/Mobile_World_Congress" title="Mobile World Congress">
           Mobile World Congress
          </a>
          (MWC), held in
          <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
           Barcelona
          </a>
          , Spain, in March 2014, which was attended by 75,000 delegates. Various media sources highlighted the connection between Facebook's focus on mobile technology and Zuckerberg's speech, stating that mobile represents the future of the company.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
           <a href="#cite_note-53">
            [53]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg's speech expands upon the goal that he raised at the
          <a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">
           TechCrunch
          </a>
          conference in September 2013, whereby he is working towards expanding Internet coverage into developing countries.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
           <a href="#cite_note-54">
            [54]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Alongside other American technology figures like
          <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">
           Jeff Bezos
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Tim_Cook" title="Tim Cook">
           Tim Cook
          </a>
          , Zuckerberg hosted visiting Chinese politician
          <a href="/wiki/Lu_Wei_(politician)" title="Lu Wei (politician)">
           Lu Wei
          </a>
          , known as the "Internet czar" for his influence in the enforcement of China's online policy, at Facebook's headquarters on December 8, 2014. The meeting occurred after Zuckerberg participated in a Q&amp;A session at
          <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">
           Tsinghua University
          </a>
          in Beijing, China, on October 23, 2014, where he conversed in
          <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">
           Mandarin Chinese
          </a>
          ; although Facebook is banned in China, Zuckerberg is highly regarded among the people and was at the university to help fuel the nation's burgeoning entrepreneur sector.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
           <a href="#cite_note-55">
            [55]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg fielded questions during a live Q&amp;A session at the company's headquarters in
          <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">
           Menlo Park
          </a>
          on December 11, 2014. The founder and CEO explained that he does not believe Facebook is a waste of time, because it facilitates social engagement, and participating in a public session was so that he could "learn how to better serve the community".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tad_56-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Tad-56">
            [56]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sam_57-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Sam-57">
            [57]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg receives a
          <a href="/wiki/One-dollar_salary" title="One-dollar salary">
           one-dollar salary
          </a>
          as CEO of Facebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-$1Club_58-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-$1Club-58">
            [58]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In June 2016,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">
            Business Insider
           </a>
          </i>
          named Zuckerberg one of the "Top 10 Business Visionaries Creating Value for the World" along with
          <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">
           Elon Musk
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Sal_Khan" title="Sal Khan">
           Sal Khan
          </a>
          , due to the fact that he and his wife "pledged to give away 99% of their wealth-then estimated at $55.0 billion".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
           <a href="#cite_note-59">
            [59]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On May 25, 2017, at Harvard's 366th commencement day, Zuckerberg, after giving a
          <a href="/wiki/Commencement_speech" title="Commencement speech">
           commencement speech
          </a>
          ,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
           <a href="#cite_note-60">
            [60]
           </a>
          </sup>
          received an honorary degree from Harvard.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
           <a href="#cite_note-61">
            [61]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
           <a href="#cite_note-62">
            [62]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In January 2019, Zuckerberg laid plans to integrate an
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/End-to-end_encrypted" title="End-to-end encrypted">
           end-to-end encrypted
          </a>
          system for three major social media platforms, including Facebook,
          <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">
           Instagram
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">
           WhatsApp
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
           <a href="#cite_note-63">
            [63]
           </a>
          </sup>
          On August 14, 2020, Facebook integrated the chat systems for Instagram and Messenger on both iOS and Android devices. The update encouraged cross-communication between Instagram and Facebook users.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
           <a href="#cite_note-64">
            [64]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Other_projects">
           Other projects
          </h3>
         </div>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Zuckerberg,_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg">
           <img alt='Waist high portrait of man in his twenties, looking into the camera and gesturing with both hands, wearing a black pullover shirt that says "The North Face" and wearing identification on a white band hanging from his neck' class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="4096" data-file-width="2711" decoding="async" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg/170px-Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg/255px-Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg/340px-Mark_Zuckerberg%2C_World_Economic_Forum_2009_Annual_Meeting.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           Zuckerberg at the
           <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">
            World Economic Forum
           </a>
           in
           <a href="/wiki/Davos" title="Davos">
            Davos
           </a>
           , Switzerland (January 2009)
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          A month after Zuckerberg launched Facebook in February 2004,
          <a href="/wiki/I2hub" title="I2hub">
           i2hub
          </a>
          , another campus-only service, created by
          <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Chang" title="Wayne Chang">
           Wayne Chang
          </a>
          and focusing on
          <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">
           peer-to-peer
          </a>
          file sharing, was launched. At the time, both i2hub and Facebook were gaining the attention of the press and growing rapidly in users and publicity. In August 2004, Zuckerberg, Andrew McCollum,
          <a href="/wiki/Adam_D%27Angelo" title="Adam D'Angelo">
           Adam D'Angelo
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Sean_Parker" title="Sean Parker">
           Sean Parker
          </a>
          launched a competing peer-to-peer file sharing service called
          <a href="/wiki/Wirehog" title="Wirehog">
           Wirehog
          </a>
          , a precursor to
          <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Platform" title="Facebook Platform">
           Facebook Platform
          </a>
          applications, which was launched in 2007.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
           <a href="#cite_note-65">
            [65]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
           <a href="#cite_note-66">
            [66]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
           <a href="#cite_note-67">
            [67]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2013, Zuckerberg launched
          <a href="/wiki/Internet.org" title="Internet.org">
           Internet.org
          </a>
          , which he described as an initiative to provide Internet access to the five billion people without it as of the launch date. The project faced significant opposition in India, where activists said its limited internet ran counter to the principle of
          <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">
           net neutrality
          </a>
          ; Zuckerberg responded by saying that a limited internet was better than no internet. Internet.org was shut down in India in February 2016, although Zuckerberg later met with Indian Prime Minister
          <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">
           Narendra Modi
          </a>
          to discuss further possibilities.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
           <a href="#cite_note-68">
            [68]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
           <a href="#cite_note-69">
            [69]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg is a board member of the
          <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">
           solar sail
          </a>
          spacecraft development project
          <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">
           Breakthrough Starshot
          </a>
          , which he co-founded with
          <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Milner" title="Yuri Milner">
           Yuri Milner
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">
           Stephen Hawking
          </a>
          in 2016.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
           <a href="#cite_note-70">
            [70]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Legal_trouble">
           Legal trouble
          </h2>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          See also:
          <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Facebook" title="Criticism of Facebook">
           Criticism of Facebook
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="ConnectU_lawsuits">
           ConnectU lawsuits
          </h3>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Main article:
          <a href="/wiki/ConnectU" title="ConnectU">
           ConnectU
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Harvard students
          <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Winklevoss" title="Cameron Winklevoss">
           Cameron Winklevoss
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Winklevoss" title="Tyler Winklevoss">
           Tyler Winklevoss
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Divya_Narendra" title="Divya Narendra">
           Divya Narendra
          </a>
          accused Zuckerberg of intentionally making them believe he would help them build a social network called HarvardConnection.com (later called
          <a href="/wiki/ConnectU" title="ConnectU">
           ConnectU
          </a>
          ).
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
           <a href="#cite_note-71">
            [71]
           </a>
          </sup>
          They filed a lawsuit in 2004; it was dismissed on a technicality on March 28, 2007. It was refiled soon thereafter in a
          <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Massachusetts" title="United States District Court for the District of Massachusetts">
           federal court
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
           Boston
          </a>
          . Facebook countersued in regards to Social Butterfly, a project put out by
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Winklevoss_Chang_Group" title="The Winklevoss Chang Group">
           The Winklevoss Chang Group
          </a>
          , an alleged partnership between ConnectU and
          <a href="/wiki/I2hub" title="I2hub">
           i2hub
          </a>
          . On June 25, 2008, the case settled and Facebook agreed to transfer over 1.2 million common shares and pay $20 million in cash.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
           <a href="#cite_note-72">
            [72]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In November 2007, confidential court documents were posted on the website of
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/02138" title="02138">
            02138
           </a>
          </i>
          , a magazine that catered to Harvard alumni. They included Zuckerberg's Social Security number, his parents' home address, and his girlfriend's address. Though Facebook filed to have the documents removed, the judge ruled in favor of
          <i>
           02138
          </i>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_73-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-73">
            [73]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Eduardo_Saverin">
           Eduardo Saverin
          </h3>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Main article:
          <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Saverin" title="Eduardo Saverin">
           Eduardo Saverin
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          In 2005, Facebook co-founder
          <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Saverin" title="Eduardo Saverin">
           Eduardo Saverin
          </a>
          filed a lawsuit against Zuckerberg and Facebook, alleging that Zuckerberg had illegally spent Saverin's money on personal expenses. The lawsuit was settled out of court and though terms of the settlement were sealed, the company affirmed Saverin's title as co-founder of Facebook, and Saverin agreed to stop talking to the press.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
           <a href="#cite_note-74">
            [74]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
           <a href="#cite_note-75">
            [75]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Pakistan_criminal_investigation">
           Pakistan criminal investigation
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          In June 2010, then Pakistani Deputy Attorney General Muhammad Azhar Sidiqque launched a criminal investigation into Zuckerberg and Facebook co-founders
          <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Moskovitz" title="Dustin Moskovitz">
           Dustin Moskovitz
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hughes" title="Chris Hughes">
           Chris Hughes
          </a>
          after a "
          <a href="/wiki/Everybody_Draw_Mohammed_Day" title="Everybody Draw Mohammed Day">
           Draw Muhammad
          </a>
          " contest was hosted on Facebook. The investigation also named the anonymous German woman who created the contest. Sidiqque asked the country's police to contact
          <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">
           Interpol
          </a>
          to have Zuckerberg and the three others arrested for
          <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy_law" title="Blasphemy law">
           blasphemy
          </a>
          . On May 19, 2010, Facebook's website was temporarily blocked in Pakistan until Facebook removed the contest from its website at the end of May. Sidiqque also asked its UN representative to raise the issue with the
          <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
           United Nations General Assembly
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
           <a href="#cite_note-76">
            [76]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
           <a href="#cite_note-77">
            [77]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Paul_Ceglia">
           Paul Ceglia
          </h3>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Main article:
          <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ceglia" title="Paul Ceglia">
           Paul Ceglia
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          In June 2010, Paul Ceglia, the owner of a wood
          <a href="/wiki/Pellet_fuel" title="Pellet fuel">
           pellet fuel
          </a>
          company in
          <a href="/wiki/Allegany_County,_New_York" title="Allegany County, New York">
           Allegany County, upstate New York
          </a>
          , filed suit against Zuckerberg, claiming 84 percent ownership of Facebook and seeking monetary damages. According to Ceglia, he and Zuckerberg signed a contract on April 28, 2003, that an initial fee of $1,000 entitled Ceglia to 50% of the website's revenue, as well as an additional 1% interest in the business per day after January 1, 2004, until website completion. Zuckerberg was developing other projects at the time, among which was
          <i>
           Facemash
          </i>
          , the predecessor to Facebook, but did not register the domain name
          <i>
           thefacebook.com
          </i>
          until January 1, 2004. The Facebook management dismissed the lawsuit as "completely frivolous". Facebook spokesman Barry Schnitt told a reporter that Ceglia's counsel had unsuccessfully sought an out-of-court settlement.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
           <a href="#cite_note-78">
            [78]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
           <a href="#cite_note-79">
            [79]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On October 26, 2012, federal authorities arrested Ceglia, charging him with mail and wire fraud and of "tampering with, destroying and fabricating evidence in a scheme to defraud the Facebook founder of billions of dollars". Ceglia is accused of fabricating emails to make it appear that he and Zuckerberg discussed details about an early version of Facebook, although after examining their emails, investigators found there was no mention of Facebook in them.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
           <a href="#cite_note-80">
            [80]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Some law firms withdrew from the case before it was initiated and others after Ceglia's arrest.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
           <a href="#cite_note-81">
            [81]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
           <a href="#cite_note-82">
            [82]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Hawaiian_land_ownership">
           Hawaiian land ownership
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          In 2014 Zuckerberg purchased 700 acres of land on the Hawaiian island of
          <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">
           Kauaʻi
          </a>
          . In January 2017, Zuckerberg filed eight "
          <a href="/wiki/Quiet_title" title="Quiet title">
           quiet title
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Partition_(law)" title="Partition (law)">
           partition
          </a>
          " lawsuits against hundreds of
          <a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">
           native Hawaiians
          </a>
          to claim small tracts of land that they owned within his acreage.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_83-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-:0-83">
            [83]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg responded to criticisms in a
          <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
           Facebook
          </a>
          post, stating that the lawsuits were a good faith effort to pay the partial owners of the land their "fair share".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_83-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-:0-83">
            [83]
           </a>
          </sup>
          When he learned that Hawaiian
          <a href="/wiki/Property_law" title="Property law">
           land ownership law
          </a>
          differs from that of the other 49 states, he dropped the lawsuits. Zuckerberg stated that he regretted not taking the time to understand the process and its history before moving ahead.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
           <a href="#cite_note-84">
            [84]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
           <a href="#cite_note-85">
            [85]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Testimony_before_U.S._Congress">
           Testimony before U.S. Congress
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          On April 10 and 11, 2018, Zuckerberg testified before the
          <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Commerce,_Science,_and_Transportation" title="United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science, and Transportation">
           United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science, and Transportation
          </a>
          regarding the usage of personal data by Facebook in relation to the
          <a href="/wiki/Facebook%E2%80%93Cambridge_Analytica_data_scandal" title="Facebook–Cambridge Analytica data scandal">
           Facebook–Cambridge Analytica data scandal
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_86-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-:1-86">
            [86]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He called the whole affair a breach of trust between
          <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Kogan_(scientist)" title="Aleksandr Kogan (scientist)">
           Aleksandr Kogan
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Analytica" title="Cambridge Analytica">
           Cambridge Analytica
          </a>
          , and Facebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
           <a href="#cite_note-87">
            [87]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg refused requests to appear to give evidence on the matter to a
          <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">
           Parliamentary
          </a>
          committee in the United Kingdom.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
           <a href="#cite_note-88">
            [88]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On October 1, 2020, the
          <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Commerce,_Science,_and_Transportation" title="United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science, and Transportation">
           US Senate Commerce Committee
          </a>
          unanimously voted to issue
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subpoenas" title="Subpoenas">
           subpoenas
          </a>
          to the CEOs of three top tech firms, including Zuckerberg,
          <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
           Google
          </a>
          's
          <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">
           Sundar Pichai
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">
           Twitter
          </a>
          's
          <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dorsey" title="Jack Dorsey">
           Jack Dorsey
          </a>
          . The subpoenas aimed to force the CEOs to testify about the legal immunity the law affords tech platforms under
          <a href="/wiki/Section_230" title="Section 230">
           Section 230 of the Communications Act
          </a>
          of 1934. US
          <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
           Republicans
          </a>
          argued that the law unduly protected social media companies against allegations of anti-conservative censorship.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
           <a href="#cite_note-89">
            [89]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On March 25, 2021, Zuckerberg testified before the House Energy and Commerce Committee regarding Facebook's role in the spread of misinformation and hate speech on the platform. During the hearing, he was questioned about Facebook's handling of user data, its role in the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2021_storming_of_the_United_States_Capitol" title="2021 storming of the United States Capitol">
           January 6, 2021, attack on the US Capitol Building
          </a>
          , and its efforts to combat misinformation and hate speech. Zuckerberg acknowledged that Facebook had a responsibility to address these issues and outlined the steps that the company is taking to improve its policies and practices. The hearing was part of a broader effort by Congress to hold tech companies accountable for their role in shaping public discourse and protecting user privacy.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
           <a href="#cite_note-90">
            [90]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In a January 2024
          <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_the_Judiciary" title="United States Senate Committee on the Judiciary">
           Senate Judiciary Committee
          </a>
          hearing on child safety and social media platforms, Zuckerberg, along with other tech CEOs, were questioned about their companies' practices. During the hearing, he apologized to the families of children who were victims of online abuse and harm.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
           <a href="#cite_note-91">
            [91]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
           <a href="#cite_note-92">
            [92]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Meta's_proposal">
           <span id="Meta.27s_proposal">
           </span>
           Meta's proposal
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          Court documents allege that Zuckerberg personally rejected Meta's proposals to improve teenagers' mental health. He consistently opposed efforts to enhance well-being on Facebook and Instagram, overriding senior executives like Instagram head
          <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mosseri" title="Adam Mosseri">
           Adam Mosseri
          </a>
          and Global Affairs President
          <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">
           Nick Clegg
          </a>
          , as revealed in an ongoing lawsuit. Internal communications disclosed in the Massachusetts-initiated legal action depict Zuckerberg's resistance to better protect over 30 million teens on Instagram in the U.S., highlighting his substantial influence on Meta's decisions impacting billions of users. These documents also shed light on occasional tensions between Zuckerberg and other Meta officials advocating for improved user well-being.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
           <a href="#cite_note-93">
            [93]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Depictions_in_media">
           Depictions in media
          </h2>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="The_Social_Network">
           <i>
            The Social Network
           </i>
          </h3>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Further information:
          <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">
           The Social Network
          </a>
         </div>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="1960" data-file-width="1326" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/170px-Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/255px-Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/340px-Jesse_Eisenberg_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Eisenberg" title="Jesse Eisenberg">
            Jesse Eisenberg
           </a>
           (pictured) played Zuckerberg in
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">
             The Social Network
            </a>
           </i>
           .
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          A movie based on Zuckerberg and the founding years of Facebook,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">
            The Social Network
           </a>
          </i>
          , was released on October 1, 2010, starring
          <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Eisenberg" title="Jesse Eisenberg">
           Jesse Eisenberg
          </a>
          as Zuckerberg. After Zuckerberg was told about the film, he responded, "I just wished that nobody made a movie of me while I was still alive".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
           <a href="#cite_note-94">
            [94]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Also, after the film's script was leaked on the Internet and it was apparent that the film would not portray Zuckerberg in a wholly positive light, he stated that he wanted to establish himself as a "good guy".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
           <a href="#cite_note-95">
            [95]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The film is based on the book
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Accidental_Billionaires" title="The Accidental Billionaires">
            The Accidental Billionaires
           </a>
          </i>
          by
          <a href="/wiki/Ben_Mezrich" title="Ben Mezrich">
           Ben Mezrich
          </a>
          , which the book's publicist once described as "big juicy fun" rather than "reportage".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
           <a href="#cite_note-96">
            [96]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The film's screenwriter
          <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sorkin" title="Aaron Sorkin">
           Aaron Sorkin
          </a>
          told
          <a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">
           <i>
            New York
           </i>
           magazine
          </a>
          , "I don't want my fidelity to be the truth; I want it to be storytelling", adding, "What is the big deal about accuracy purely for accuracy's sake, and can we not have the true be the enemy of the good?"
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
           <a href="#cite_note-97">
            [97]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Upon winning the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">
           Golden Globe Award
          </a>
          for Best Picture on January 16, 2011, producer
          <a href="/wiki/Scott_Rudin" title="Scott Rudin">
           Scott Rudin
          </a>
          thanked Facebook and Zuckerberg "for his willingness to allow us to use his life and work as a
          <a href="/wiki/Metaphor" title="Metaphor">
           metaphor
          </a>
          through which to tell a story about communication and the way we relate to each other".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
           <a href="#cite_note-98">
            [98]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Sorkin, who won for Best Screenplay, retracted some of the impressions given in his script:
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
           <a href="#cite_note-99">
            [99]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           I wanted to say to Mark Zuckerberg tonight, if you're watching,
           <a href="/wiki/Rooney_Mara" title="Rooney Mara">
            Rooney Mara
           </a>
           's character makes a prediction at the beginning of the movie. She was wrong. You turned out to be a great entrepreneur, a visionary, and an incredible altruist.
          </dd>
         </dl>
         <p>
          In January 2011, Zuckerberg made a surprise guest appearance on
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">
            Saturday Night Live
           </a>
          </i>
          , which was hosted by Jesse Eisenberg. They both said it was the first time they had met.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
           <a href="#cite_note-100">
            [100]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Eisenberg asked Zuckerberg, who had been critical of his portrayal by the film, what he thought of the movie. Zuckerberg replied, "It was interesting".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
           <a href="#cite_note-101">
            [101]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In a subsequent interview about their meeting, Eisenberg explained that he was "nervous to meet him, because I had spent now, a year and a half thinking about him "... He added, "Mark has been so gracious about something that's really so uncomfortable ... The fact that he would do
          <i>
           SNL
          </i>
          and make fun of the situation is so sweet and so generous. It's the best possible way to handle something that, I think, could otherwise be very uncomfortable".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
           <a href="#cite_note-102">
            [102]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
           <a href="#cite_note-103">
            [103]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading4">
          <h4 id="Disputed_accuracy">
           Disputed accuracy
          </h4>
         </div>
         <p>
          According to
          <a href="/wiki/David_Kirkpatrick_(author)" title="David Kirkpatrick (author)">
           David Kirkpatrick
          </a>
          , former technology editor at
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">
            Fortune
           </a>
          </i>
          magazine and author of
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Facebook_Effect:_The_Inside_Story_of_the_Company_that_is_Connecting_the_World" title="The Facebook Effect: The Inside Story of the Company that is Connecting the World">
            The Facebook Effect: The Inside Story of the Company that is Connecting the World
           </a>
          </i>
          (2011),
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
           <a href="#cite_note-104">
            [104]
           </a>
          </sup>
          "the film is only 40% true ... he is not snide and sarcastic in a cruel way, the way Zuckerberg is played in the movie". He says that "a lot of the factual incidents are accurate, but many are distorted and the overall impression is false", and concludes that primarily "his motivations were to try and come up with a new way to share information on the Internet".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCmovie_105-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-BBCmovie-105">
            [105]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Although the film portrayed Zuckerberg's creation of Facebook in order to elevate his stature after not getting into any of the elite
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Officially_unrecognized_Harvard_College_social_clubs" title="Officially unrecognized Harvard College social clubs">
           final clubs
          </a>
          at Harvard, Zuckerberg stated that he had no interest in joining the clubs.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEWYORKER2010_5-5">
           <a href="#cite_note-NEWYORKER2010-5">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Kirkpatrick agreed that the impression implied by the film is "false". Karel Baloun, a former senior engineer at Facebook, noted that the "image of Zuckerberg as a socially inept nerd is overstated ... It is fiction "... He likewise dismissed the film's assertion that he "would deliberately betray a friend".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCmovie_105-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-BBCmovie-105">
            [105]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Other_depictions">
           Other depictions
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg voiced himself on an episode of
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">
            The Simpsons
           </a>
          </i>
          titled "
          <a href="/wiki/Loan-a_Lisa" title="Loan-a Lisa">
           Loan-a Lisa
          </a>
          ", which first aired on October 3, 2010. In the episode,
          <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Simpson" title="Lisa Simpson">
           Lisa Simpson
          </a>
          and her friend Nelson encounter Zuckerberg at an entrepreneurs' convention. Zuckerberg tells Lisa that she does not need to graduate from college to be wildly successful, referencing
          <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">
           Bill Gates
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">
           Richard Branson
          </a>
          as examples.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
           <a href="#cite_note-106">
            [106]
           </a>
          </sup>
          On October 9, 2010,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">
            Saturday Night Live
           </a>
          </i>
          lampooned Zuckerberg and Facebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
           <a href="#cite_note-107">
            [107]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <a href="/wiki/Andy_Samberg" title="Andy Samberg">
           Andy Samberg
          </a>
          portrayed the role of Zuckerberg. Zuckerberg himself was reported to have been amused: "I thought this was funny".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
           <a href="#cite_note-108">
            [108]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">
           Stephen Colbert
          </a>
          awarded a "Medal of Fear" to Zuckerberg at the
