          <a href="/wiki/Rally_to_Restore_Sanity_and/or_Fear" title="Rally to Restore Sanity and/or Fear">
           Rally to Restore Sanity and/or Fear
          </a>
          on October 30, 2010, "because he values his privacy much more than he values yours".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
           <a href="#cite_note-109">
            [109]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg appeared in the climax of 2013 documentary film
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Terms_and_Conditions_May_Apply" title="Terms and Conditions May Apply">
            Terms and Conditions May Apply
           </a>
          </i>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
           <a href="#cite_note-110">
            [110]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
           <a href="#cite_note-111">
            [111]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
           <a href="#cite_note-112">
            [112]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">
            South Park
           </a>
          </i>
          episode "
          <a href="/wiki/Franchise_Prequel" title="Franchise Prequel">
           Franchise Prequel
          </a>
          " mocked him. According to
          <a href="/wiki/CNET" title="CNET">
           CNET
          </a>
          , he was portrayed as "a rosy-cheeked bully nerd who utters strange noises, makes peculiar kung fu gestures and turns up wherever he likes in people's houses".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
           <a href="#cite_note-113">
            [113]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Donations_and_Chan_Zuckerberg_Initiative">
           Donations and Chan Zuckerberg Initiative
          </h2>
         </div>
         <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
         <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
          Further information:
          <a href="/wiki/Chan_Zuckerberg_Initiative" title="Chan Zuckerberg Initiative">
           Chan Zuckerberg Initiative
          </a>
         </div>
         <figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg/170px-Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg/255px-Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg/340px-Mark_Zuckerberg_in_Prague_2013.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           Zuckerberg and his wife
           <a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Chan" title="Priscilla Chan">
            Priscilla Chan
           </a>
           in May 2013
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg founded the
          <a href="/wiki/Startup:Education" title="Startup:Education">
           Startup:Education
          </a>
          foundation.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
           <a href="#cite_note-114">
            [114]
           </a>
          </sup>
          It was reported in September 2010 that he had donated $100 million to
          <a href="/wiki/Newark_Public_Schools" title="Newark Public Schools">
           Newark Public Schools
          </a>
          , the public school system of
          <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">
           Newark, New Jersey
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
           <a href="#cite_note-115">
            [115]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
           <a href="#cite_note-116">
            [116]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Critics noted the timing of the donation as being close to the release of
          <i>
           The Social Network
          </i>
          , which painted a somewhat negative portrait of Zuckerberg.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
           <a href="#cite_note-117">
            [117]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg responded to the criticism, saying, "The thing that I was most sensitive about with the movie timing was, I didn't want the press about
          <i>
           The Social Network
          </i>
          movie to get conflated with the Newark project. I was thinking about doing this anonymously just so that the two things could be kept separate".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes20100924_118-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-forbes20100924-118">
            [118]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Newark Mayor
          <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">
           Cory Booker
          </a>
          stated that he and New Jersey Governor
          <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">
           Chris Christie
          </a>
          had to convince Zuckerberg's team not to make the donation anonymously.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes20100924_118-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-forbes20100924-118">
            [118]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The money was largely wasted, according to journalist Dale Russakoff.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
           <a href="#cite_note-119">
            [119]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
           <a href="#cite_note-120">
            [120]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2010, Zuckerberg,
          <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">
           Bill Gates
          </a>
          , and investor
          <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">
           Warren Buffett
          </a>
          signed
          <a href="/wiki/The_Giving_Pledge" title="The Giving Pledge">
           The Giving Pledge
          </a>
          , in which they said they would donate to charity at least half of their wealth over the course of time, and invited others among the wealthy to donate 50 percent or more of their wealth to charity.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
           <a href="#cite_note-121">
            [121]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In December 2012, Zuckerberg and his wife
          <a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Chan" title="Priscilla Chan">
           Priscilla Chan
          </a>
          said that over the course of their lives they would give the majority of their wealth to "advancing human potential and promoting equality" in the spirit of The Giving Pledge.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
           <a href="#cite_note-122">
            [122]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
           <a href="#cite_note-123">
            [123]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In December 2013, Zuckerberg announced a donation of 18 million Facebook shares to the
          <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley_Community_Foundation" title="Silicon Valley Community Foundation">
           Silicon Valley Community Foundation
          </a>
          , to be executed by the end of the month—based on Facebook's valuation as of then, the shares totaled $990 million in value. Later that month, the donation was recognized as the largest charitable gift on public record for that year.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
           <a href="#cite_note-124">
            [124]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Chronicle_of_Philanthropy" title="The Chronicle of Philanthropy">
            The Chronicle of Philanthropy
           </a>
          </i>
          placed Zuckerberg and his wife at the top of the magazine's annual list of 50 most generous Americans for 2013, having donated roughly $1 billion to charity.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usa-today-biggest-giver_125-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-usa-today-biggest-giver-125">
            [125]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In October 2014, Zuckerberg and his wife donated $25 million to combat the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease" title="Ebola virus disease">
           Ebola virus disease
          </a>
          , specifically the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_African_Ebola_virus_epidemic" title="West African Ebola virus epidemic">
           West African Ebola virus epidemic
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
           <a href="#cite_note-126">
            [126]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
           <a href="#cite_note-127">
            [127]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The couple endowed the foundation of the
          <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_General_Hospital" title="San Francisco General Hospital">
           San Francisco General Hospital
          </a>
          in February 2015 with $75 million, which was the biggest individual donation to a U.S. public hospital. The hospital honored them by renaming itself as The Priscilla Chan and Mark Zuckerberg San Francisco General Hospital and Trauma Center. Later in 2020, the
          <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Board_of_Supervisors" title="San Francisco Board of Supervisors">
           San Francisco Board of Supervisors
          </a>
          passed a near-unanimous, non-binding measure condemning the renaming, citing concerns that a public hospital should not be named after an individual whose social media platform is accused of "endangering public health, spreading misinformation, and violating privacy".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
           <a href="#cite_note-128">
            [128]
           </a>
          </sup>
          On December 1, 2015, the couple pledged to transfer 99% of their Facebook shares, then valued at $45 billion, to the
          <a href="/wiki/Chan_Zuckerberg_Initiative" title="Chan Zuckerberg Initiative">
           Chan Zuckerberg Initiative
          </a>
          (CZI).
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
           <a href="#cite_note-129">
            [129]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The funds would not be transferred immediately, but over the course of their lives.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_1_December_2015_130-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_1_December_2015-130">
            [130]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Instead of forming a charitable corporation to donate the value of the stock to, as
          <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">
           Bill Gates
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">
           Warren Buffett
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">
           Larry Page
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">
           Sergey Brin
          </a>
          and other billionaires have done, Zuckerberg and Chan chose to use the structure of a
          <a href="/wiki/Limited_liability_company" title="Limited liability company">
           limited liability company (LLC)
          </a>
          . Some journalists and academics have said the CZI conducts
          <a href="/wiki/Philanthrocapitalism" title="Philanthrocapitalism">
           philanthrocapitalism
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
           <a href="#cite_note-131">
            [131]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
           <a href="#cite_note-132">
            [132]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
           <a href="#cite_note-133">
            [133]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2016, CZI gave $600 million to create the tax-exempt charity
          <a href="/wiki/Chan_Zuckerberg_Biohub" title="Chan Zuckerberg Biohub">
           Chan Zuckerberg Biohub
          </a>
          , a collaborative research space in San Francisco's
          <a href="/wiki/Mission_Bay,_San_Francisco" title="Mission Bay, San Francisco">
           Mission Bay district
          </a>
          near the
          <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Francisco" title="University of California, San Francisco">
           University of California, San Francisco
          </a>
          , with the intent to foster interaction and collaboration between scientists at UCSF,
          <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">
           University of California, Berkeley
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">
           Stanford University
          </a>
          . Intellectual property generated would be jointly owned by Biohub and the discoverer's home institution. Unlike foundations like the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">
           Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation
          </a>
          which open up all research funded to unrestricted access and reuse by the public, Biohub retained the right to commercialize any research it funds. Inventors will have the option of making their discoveries open-source, with permission from Biohub.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
           <a href="#cite_note-134">
            [134]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
           <a href="#cite_note-135">
            [135]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
           <a href="#cite_note-136">
            [136]
           </a>
          </sup>
          To increase access to scientific research and promote open science, CZ Biohub requires its investigators and staff scientists to publish submitted manuscripts and related data on
          <a href="/wiki/Preprint" title="Preprint">
           preprints
          </a>
          servers like
          <a href="/wiki/BioRxiv" title="BioRxiv">
           bioRxiv
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
           <a href="#cite_note-137">
            [137]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
           <a href="#cite_note-138">
            [138]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Amidst the
          <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">
           COVID-19 pandemic
          </a>
          , Zuckerberg donated $25 million to a
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">
           Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation
          </a>
          -backed accelerator that is searching for treatments for the disease.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
           <a href="#cite_note-139">
            [139]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He also announced $25 million in grants to support local journalism that was impacted by the pandemic and $75 million in advertisement purchases in local newspapers by
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Facebook,_Inc." title="Facebook, Inc.">
           Facebook, Inc.
          </a>
          , where Facebook would market itself.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
           <a href="#cite_note-140">
            [140]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Politics">
           Politics
          </h2>
         </div>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="2571" data-file-width="3908" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg/220px-Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg/330px-Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg/440px-Zuckerberg_meets_Obama.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           With
           <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
            Barack Obama
           </a>
           before a private meeting between Obama and technology business leaders in February 2011
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          In 2002, Zuckerberg registered to vote in
          <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">
           Westchester County, New York
          </a>
          , where he grew up, but did not cast a ballot until November 2008. Then
          <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">
           Santa Clara County
          </a>
          Registrar of Voters Spokeswoman, Elma Rosas, told Bloomberg that Zuckerberg is listed as "no preference" on voter rolls, and he voted in at least two of the past three general elections, in
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_elections,_2008" title="United States elections, 2008">
           2008
          </a>
          and
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_elections,_2012" title="United States elections, 2012">
           2012
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
           <a href="#cite_note-141">
            [141]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
           <a href="#cite_note-142">
            [142]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg has never revealed his own political affiliation or voting history: some news outlets consider him to be a
          <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">
           conservative
          </a>
          ,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
           <a href="#cite_note-143">
            [143]
           </a>
          </sup>
          while others consider him
          <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">
           liberal
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
           <a href="#cite_note-144">
            [144]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In February 2013, Zuckerberg hosted his first ever fundraising event for then New Jersey Governor
          <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">
           Chris Christie
          </a>
          . His particular interest on this occasion was education reform, and Christie's education reform work focused on teachers unions and the expansion of charter schools.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
           <a href="#cite_note-145">
            [145]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
           <a href="#cite_note-146">
            [146]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Later that year, Zuckerberg hosted a campaign fundraiser for then Newark mayor
          <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">
           Cory Booker
          </a>
          , who was running in the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_special_election_in_New_Jersey,_2013" title="United States Senate special election in New Jersey, 2013">
           2013 New Jersey special Senate election
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
           <a href="#cite_note-147">
            [147]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In September 2010, with the support of Governor Chris Christie, Booker obtained a US$100 million pledge from Zuckerberg to
          <a href="/wiki/Newark_Public_Schools" title="Newark Public Schools">
           Newark Public Schools
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
           <a href="#cite_note-148">
            [148]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In December 2012, Zuckerberg donated 18 million shares to the
          <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley_Community_Foundation" title="Silicon Valley Community Foundation">
           Silicon Valley Community Foundation
          </a>
          , a community organization that includes education in its list of grant-making areas.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-education_149-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-education-149">
            [149]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mercury-news-achievement-gap_150-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-mercury-news-achievement-gap-150">
            [150]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="1940" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg/220px-Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg/330px-Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg/440px-Cristina_Kirchner_and_Mark_Zuckerberg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           With then Argentine President
           <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">
            Cristina Fernández de Kirchner
           </a>
           in April 2015
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          On April 11, 2013, Zuckerberg led the launch of a
          <a href="/wiki/501(c)_organization" title="501(c) organization">
           501(c)(4) lobbying group
          </a>
          called
          <a href="/wiki/FWD.us" title="FWD.us">
           FWD.us
          </a>
          . The founders and contributors to the group were primarily Silicon Valley entrepreneurs and investors, and its president was
          <a href="/wiki/Joe_Green_(entrepreneur)" title="Joe Green (entrepreneur)">
           Joe Green
          </a>
          , a close friend of Zuckerberg.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fwd-us-techcrunch1_151-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fwd-us-techcrunch1-151">
            [151]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fwd-us-techcrunch2_152-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fwd-us-techcrunch2-152">
            [152]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The goals of the group include
          <a href="/wiki/Immigration_reform" title="Immigration reform">
           immigration reform
          </a>
          , improving the state of education in the United States, and enabling more technological breakthroughs that benefit the public,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fwd-us-zuck-op-ed_153-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fwd-us-zuck-op-ed-153">
            [153]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fwd-us-about-us_154-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fwd-us-about-us-154">
            [154]
           </a>
          </sup>
          yet it has also been criticized for financing ads advocating a variety of oil and gas development initiatives, including drilling in the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge and the Keystone XL pipeline.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zuckerberg_takes_heat_155-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-zuckerberg_takes_heat-155">
            [155]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In 2013, numerous liberal and progressive groups, such as
          <a href="/wiki/League_of_Conservation_Voters" title="League of Conservation Voters">
           The League of Conservation Voters
          </a>
          ,
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MoveOn.org" title="MoveOn.org">
           MoveOn.org
          </a>
          , the
          <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">
           Sierra Club
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Democracy_for_America" title="Democracy for America">
           Democracy for America
          </a>
          , CREDO,
          <a href="/wiki/Daily_Kos" title="Daily Kos">
           Daily Kos
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/350.org" title="350.org">
           350.org
          </a>
          , and Presente and Progressives United agreed to either pull their Facebook ad buys or not buy Facebook ads for at least two weeks, in protest of Zuckerberg ads funded by FWD.us that were in support of oil drilling and the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keystone_XL" title="Keystone XL">
           Keystone XL pipeline
          </a>
          , and in opposition to
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">
           Obamacare
          </a>
          among Republican United States senators who back immigration reform.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
           <a href="#cite_note-156">
            [156]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          A media report on June 20, 2013, revealed that Zuckerberg actively engaged with Facebook users on his own profile page after the online publication of a FWD.us video. In response to a claim that the FWD.us organization is "just about tech wanting to hire more people", the Internet entrepreneur replied: "The bigger problem we're trying to address is ensuring the 11 million undocumented folks living in this country now and similar folks in the future are treated fairly".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
           <a href="#cite_note-157">
            [157]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In June 2013, Zuckerberg joined Facebook employees in a company float as part of the annual
          <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Pride" title="San Francisco Pride">
           San Francisco Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, and Transgender Pride Celebration
          </a>
          . The company first participated in the event in 2011, with 70 employees, and this number increased to 700 for the 2013 march. The 2013 pride celebration was especially significant, as it followed a
          <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">
           U.S. Supreme Court
          </a>
          ruling that deemed the
          <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">
           Defense of Marriage Act
          </a>
          (DOMA) unconstitutional.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
           <a href="#cite_note-158">
            [158]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
           <a href="#cite_note-159">
            [159]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_(48765153148).jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg/220px-President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg/330px-President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg/440px-President_Trump_Meets_with_Mark_Zuckerberg_%2848765153148%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           With then President
           <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">
            Donald Trump
           </a>
           at the White House in September 2019
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          When questioned about the mid-2013
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">
           PRISM
          </a>
          scandal at the TechCrunch Disrupt conference in September 2013, Zuckerberg stated that the U.S. government "blew it". He further explained that the government performed poorly in regard to the protection of the freedoms of its citizens, the economy, and companies.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Six_51-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Six-51">
            [51]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg placed a statement on his Facebook wall on December 9, 2015, which said that he wants "to add my voice in support of Muslims in our community and around the world" in response to the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_presidential_campaign,_2016#Policies_targeting_Muslims" title="Donald Trump presidential campaign, 2016">
           aftermath
          </a>
          of the
          <a href="/wiki/November_2015_Paris_attacks" title="November 2015 Paris attacks">
           November 2015 Paris attacks
          </a>
          and the
          <a href="/wiki/2015_San_Bernardino_attack" title="2015 San Bernardino attack">
           2015 San Bernardino attack
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-protect_160-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-protect-160">
            [160]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbpost2015_161-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-fbpost2015-161">
            [161]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gd1215_162-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-gd1215-162">
            [162]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yt1215_163-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-yt1215-163">
            [163]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The statement also said that Muslims are "always welcome" on Facebook, and that his position was a result of the fact that "
          <a href="/wiki/Jewish_culture" title="Jewish culture">
           as a Jew
          </a>
          , my parents taught me that we must stand up against attacks on all communities".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haar1215_164-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-haar1215-164">
            [164]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ind1215_165-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-ind1215-165">
            [165]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          On February 24, 2016, Zuckerberg sent out a company-wide internal memo to employees formally rebuking employees who had crossed out handwritten "
          <a href="/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter" title="Black Lives Matter">
           Black Lives Matter
          </a>
          " phrases on the company walls and had written "All Lives Matter" in their place. Facebook allows employees to free-write thoughts and phrases on company walls. The memo was then leaked by several employees. As Zuckerberg had previously condemned this practice at previous company meetings, and other similar requests had been issued by other leaders at Facebook, Zuckerberg wrote in the memo that he would now consider this overwriting practice not only disrespectful, but "malicious as well". According to Zuckerberg's memo, "
          <i>
           Black Lives Matter
          </i>
          doesn't mean other lives don't – it's simply asking that the black community also achieves the justice they deserve". The memo also noted that the act of crossing something out in itself, "means silencing speech, or that one person's speech is more important than another's". Zuckerberg also said in the memo that he would be launching investigations into the incidents.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shaunking-zuckerberg_166-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-shaunking-zuckerberg-166">
            [166]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guynn_167-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-guynn-167">
            [167]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-benjaminsnyder_168-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-benjaminsnyder-168">
            [168]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">
            New York Daily News
           </a>
          </i>
          interviewed Facebook employees who commented anonymously that, "Zuckerberg was genuinely angry about the incident and it really encouraged staff that Zuckerberg showed a clear understanding of why the phrase 'Black Lives Matter' must exist, as well as why writing through it is a form of harassment and erasure".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shaunking-zuckerberg_166-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-shaunking-zuckerberg-166">
            [166]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In January 2017, Zuckerberg criticized Donald Trump's
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_order_(United_States)" title="Executive order (United States)">
           executive order
          </a>
          to severely limit immigrants and refugees from some countries.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
           <a href="#cite_note-169">
            [169]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He also funded a state-level ballot initiative for the
          <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_elections" title="2020 United States elections">
           2020 general election
          </a>
          that would raise taxes by altering California's
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Split_roll" title="Split roll">
           Proposition 13
          </a>
          to require the tax assessment of commercial and industrial properties in the state at market rate.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
           <a href="#cite_note-170">
            [170]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">
          <h2 id="Personal_life">
           Personal life
          </h2>
         </div>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Marriage_and_children">
           Marriage and children
          </h3>
         </div>
         <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">
          <a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._(15150761882)_(cropped).jpg">
           <img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="310" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._%2815150761882%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._%2815150761882%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._%2815150761882%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._%2815150761882%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Visita_de_Mark_Zuckerberg_a_Los_Pinos._%2815150761882%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           With his wife, Priscilla Chan, in 2014
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          Zuckerberg met fellow
          <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">
           Harvard
          </a>
          student
          <a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Chan" title="Priscilla Chan">
           Priscilla Chan
          </a>
          at a frat party during his sophomore year with whom he began dating in 2003.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes1_171-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-forbes1-171">
            [171]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In September 2010, Chan, who was a medical student at the
          <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Francisco" title="University of California, San Francisco">
           University of California, San Francisco
          </a>
          at the time,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
           <a href="#cite_note-172">
            [172]
           </a>
          </sup>
          moved into his rented house in
          <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">
           Palo Alto, California
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
           <a href="#cite_note-173">
            [173]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
           <a href="#cite_note-174">
            [174]
           </a>
          </sup>
          They married on May 19, 2012, in the grounds of his mansion in an event that also celebrated her graduation from medical school.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
           <a href="#cite_note-175">
            [175]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
           <a href="#cite_note-176">
            [176]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg revealed on July 31, 2015, that they were expecting a baby girl and that Chan had previously experienced three miscarriages.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
           <a href="#cite_note-177">
            [177]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Their daughter, Maxima Chan Zuckerberg, was born on December 1, 2015.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
           <a href="#cite_note-178">
            [178]
           </a>
          </sup>
          They announced in a
          <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">
           Chinese New Year
          </a>
          video that their daughter's Chinese name is Chen Mingyu (
          <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
           Chinese
          </a>
          :
          <span lang="zh">
           陈明宇
          </span>
          ).
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
           <a href="#cite_note-179">
            [179]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Their second daughter, August, was born in August 2017.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
           <a href="#cite_note-180">
            [180]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Zuckerberg and his wife welcomed their third daughter Aurelia on March 24, 2023, and announced the news across his social media pages.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
           <a href="#cite_note-181">
            [181]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The couple also have a
          <a href="/wiki/Puli_dog" title="Puli dog">
           Puli dog
          </a>
          named Beast,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
           <a href="#cite_note-182">
            [182]
           </a>
          </sup>
          who has over two million followers on Facebook.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
           <a href="#cite_note-183">
            [183]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Recognition">
           Recognition
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">
           <i>
            Time
           </i>
          </a>
          named Zuckerberg
          <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">
           one of the most influential people in the world
          </a>
          in 2008, 2011, 2016 and 2019, and nominated him as a finalist several other times. He was named the
          <a href="/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year" title="Time Person of the Year">
           <i>
            Time
           </i>
           Person of the Year
          </a>
          in 2010, the same year when Facebook eclipsed more than half a billion users.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
           <a href="#cite_note-184">
            [184]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In December 2016, Zuckerberg was ranked tenth on the
          <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_the_World%27s_Most_Powerful_People" title="Forbes list of the World's Most Powerful People">
           Forbes list of the World's Most Powerful People
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
           <a href="#cite_note-185">
            [185]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In the
          <a href="/wiki/Forbes_400" title="Forbes 400">
           <i>
            Forbes
           </i>
           400
          </a>
          list of wealthiest Americans in 2023, he was ranked eighth with a personal wealth of $106 billion.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
           <a href="#cite_note-186">
            [186]
           </a>
          </sup>
          As of May 2024
          <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
           <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mark_Zuckerberg&amp;action=edit">
            [update]
           </a>
          </sup>
          , Zuckerberg's net worth was estimated at $166 billion by
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">
            Forbes
           </a>
          </i>
          , making him the fourth richest person in the world.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
           <a href="#cite_note-187">
            [187]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading3">
          <h3 id="Religious_beliefs_and_other_interests">
           Religious beliefs and other interests
          </h3>
         </div>
         <p>
          Raised as a Reform Jew, Zuckerberg later identified as an atheist. However, he said in 2016 that "I went through a period where I questioned things, but now I believe religion is very important".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirkpatrick_7-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Kirkpatrick-7">
            [7]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
           <a href="#cite_note-188">
            [188]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
           <a href="#cite_note-189">
            [189]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In 2017, he and his wife began a nationwide tour "to visit every state in the union and learn more about a sliver of the nearly two billion people who regularly use the social network". He met with farmers and business owners, and spoke at
          <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Emanuel African Methodist Episcopal Church">
           Mother Emanuel
          </a>
          , where
          <a href="/wiki/Charleston_church_shooting" title="Charleston church shooting">
           a shooting
          </a>
          took place in 2015.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
           <a href="#cite_note-190">
            [190]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
           <a href="#cite_note-191">
            [191]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In an August 2022 appearance on
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/The_Joe_Rogan_Experience" title="The Joe Rogan Experience">
            The Joe Rogan Experience
           </a>
          </i>
          , Zuckerberg said one of his biggest regrets was competing on the fencing team in high school instead of wrestling.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
           <a href="#cite_note-192">
            [192]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2022, Zuckerberg took up training in both
          <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">
           mixed martial arts
          </a>
          (MMA) and
          <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_jiu-jitsu" title="Brazilian jiu-jitsu">
           Brazilian jiu-jitsu
          </a>
          (BJJ), and has been open about his love for the two sports.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
           <a href="#cite_note-193">
            [193]
           </a>
          </sup>
          He competed in a BJJ tournament on May 6, 2023, and won both a silver and gold medal in
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BJJ_gi" title="BJJ gi">
           gi
          </a>
          and no gi, competing at white belt.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
           <a href="#cite_note-194">
            [194]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In July 2023, he was promoted to
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BJJ_belt" title="BJJ belt">
           blue belt
          </a>
          in Brazilian jiu-jitsu by Dave Camarillo.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
           <a href="#cite_note-195">
            [195]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Four months later, Zuckerberg announced that he was preparing to make his MMA debut but had suffered an
          <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cruciate_ligament_injury" title="Anterior cruciate ligament injury">
           anterior cruciate ligament injury
          </a>
          in training that required surgery and had delayed this.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
           <a href="#cite_note-196">
            [196]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">

           See also
          </h2>
         </div>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg_book_club" title="Mark Zuckerberg book club">
            Mark Zuckerberg book club
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
